# Completed Tasks

## 2026-04-17

- [x] SEC-H63. **Transactional stocktake commit with `WHERE status='open'` guard inside txn.** Pre-fix: `POST /stocktake/:id/commit` at `packages/server/src/routes/stocktake.routes.ts:266-347` did a pre-txn `SELECT status` + `if (session.status !== 'open') throw`, then opened `db.transaction()` that (a) looped stocktake_counts updating `inventory_items.in_stock = ?` + inserting `stock_movements`, and (b) as the LAST txn statement flipped `stocktakes.status='committed'`. Two concurrent commit POSTs could both pass the pre-txn "is open" check (because the winner hadn't opened its txn yet), both enter their own transactions, both apply every variance — double-adjusting every `in_stock` and double-writing `stock_movements` for every counted item. Partial failure after the stock writes would also have left the status='open' momentarily until the final UPDATE (minor — the txn would roll it back anyway, but the ordering encoded no intent). Post-fix: moved the status flip to the FIRST mutation inside the single `db.transaction()` block and made it a conditional UPDATE: `UPDATE stocktakes SET status='committed', committed_at=datetime('now'), committed_by_user_id=? WHERE id=? AND status='open'`. Asserts `lockResult.changes === 1`; on `0`, sets `raceLost = true` and throws `AppError 409 'Stocktake is already being committed or was just closed'`. better-sqlite3's `transaction(fn)` wraps `BEGIN...COMMIT` and better-sqlite3 is synchronous — so the `WHERE status='open'` predicate and the subsequent `UPDATE inventory_items` / `INSERT stock_movements` statements execute as an indivisible unit. A concurrent commit reaching its own txn sees the winner's already-committed `status='committed'`, its conditional UPDATE returns `changes=0`, the txn throws, rolls back, and returns 409. Because the status flip is INSIDE the txn, any mid-txn error (item went inactive, disk full, crash) rolls back everything — including the status flip — so the session returns to `status='open'` for a clean retry rather than being stuck in a half-committed state. The task description suggested a `'committing'` intermediate status, but migration 091 defines the schema `CHECK (status IN ('open', 'committed', 'cancelled'))` — a third state would need a new migration. Folding the race guard directly into the `'open' → 'committed'` transition within the atomic txn achieves the same guarantee with less schema churn. Also added a `stocktake_commit_failed` audit event in the catch block with `{stocktake_id, race_lost, reason}` so race-loss AND any other mid-txn failure surface in `audit_log` — previously only `stocktake_committed` (success) was audited, so a rolled-back commit left no forensic trail. Verified: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` → clean (zero errors). Files modified: `packages/server/src/routes/stocktake.routes.ts` (~40 net insertions, reordered one existing UPDATE). (BH-B-011). Commit 212c917.

- [x] PROD99. **Crash recovery: uncaught exceptions logged + process restarts — verified.** Verification-only. Read `packages/server/src/index.ts:3081-3247`. Key evidence: (a) `handleFatal(type, error)` at line 3186 logs the fatal error via `log.error('FATAL: unrecoverable process error — initiating shutdown', { type, route, errorName, errorMessage, stack })`, then calls `recordCrash()` (tracker), `emitCrashLog()` (JSON file at `packages/server/data/crash-log.json`), and `broadcast('management:crash', entry)` so any connected management dashboards see it immediately. (b) Installs a 10s force-exit timer via `setTimeout(() => process.exit(1), 10000)` so a wedged shutdown cannot leave a zombie. (c) Calls `shutdown(type)` which — per line 3081 comment — "exit with code 1 so PM2/systemd treats as a failed run worth restarting". (d) Both handlers wired: `process.on('uncaughtException', ...)` at line 3240, `process.on('unhandledRejection', ...)` at line 3244. Neither path ever silently swallows — every branch either logs before exit or fires `recordCrash()` before exit. `ecosystem.config.js` at repo root configures PM2 to restart on non-zero exit.

- [x] PROD100. **`/health` endpoint LB-probe-suitable — verified.** Verification-only. The endpoint is named `/health` + `/api/v1/health`, not `/healthz` — naming delta only, functionality matches the PROD100 acceptance criteria. Read `packages/server/src/index.ts:1472-1495`: `probeMasterDb()` runs a single `db.prepare('SELECT 1').get()` round-trip; both `GET /health` and `GET /api/v1/health` return `{success:true,data:{status:'ok'}}` on 200 when the probe succeeds, or `503 {success:false,message:'db unreachable'}` when it fails. Comment at line 1457 notes the pre-PROD100 routes used to return heap/rss/DB-size/worker-queue-depth/uptime/version/timestamp — that info leak was split into `/api/v1/health/internal` (admin-only) so the public probe is now lean. `requestLogger` skips `/health` + `/api/v1/health` + `/favicon.ico` to prevent log spam from LB probes (`middleware/requestLogger.ts:49`). `tenantResolver` also skips the health paths so multi-tenant subdomain resolution doesn't block probes (`middleware/tenantResolver.ts:364-365`). Suitable for any LB backend-health probe configuration.

- [x] PROD101. **`/readyz` checks DB connectivity — verified.** Verification-only. The endpoint is named `/api/v1/health/ready`, not `/readyz` — naming delta only, functionality matches acceptance criteria. Read `packages/server/src/index.ts:1502-1531`: (a) returns `503 {success:false,message:'Server is still starting'}` while the global `isReady` boot flag is false (set to true only after `migrateAllTenants()` resolves, per comment at line 1497-1501). (b) Once ready, runs a second DB round-trip via `db.prepare('PRAGMA user_version').get()` to catch post-boot DB degradation (file pulled out, schema migration in flight, WAL corruption). On prepare/get failure, returns `503 {success:false,message:'db unreachable'}` so orchestrators drain traffic instead of sending requests that will 500. (c) On success, returns 200 with `{status:'ready', degraded: readyError !== null, schemaVersion: userVersion}` — the `degraded` flag flips to true when per-tenant migrations had partial failures but core is usable, giving orchestrators a three-way signal (healthy / degraded / unreachable). Suitable for K8s readiness probe / LB activation-gate configuration.

- [x] PROD116. **Migration prefix collision handled safely — verified.** Verification-only. Read `packages/server/src/db/migrate.ts` end-to-end (81 lines). (a) The `_migrations` tracking table at line 10-16 defines `name TEXT NOT NULL UNIQUE` — full filename is the PK, not just the numeric prefix, so `049_customer_is_active.sql` + `049_po_status_workflow.sql` + `049_sms_scheduled_and_archival.sql` each get their own row. (b) `readdirSync(migrationsDir).filter(f => f.endsWith('.sql')).sort()` at line 24-26 — JS `Array.prototype.sort()` with no comparator defaults to UTF-16 lexicographic, which is deterministic across the three 049 files (`c < p < s` on the char-17 position) and the two 050 files (`a < l`). Rerun on any OS: identical order. (c) Per-migration execution at line 32-63 reads the full filename's applied-status against the `applied` Set built from `_migrations.name`, so a missing migration re-runs while applied ones skip. (d) INSERT INTO _migrations at line 53 / 60 uses the full filename; a duplicate INSERT would throw on the UNIQUE constraint and fail the migration transaction loudly — no silent skip path. (e) Migration fail handler at line 65-69 rethrows with a descriptive message — zero swallow. Conclusion: collisions are cosmetic filename artifacts; migrate.ts handles them correctly.

- [x] PROD59. **Self-service tenant termination — multi-step-confirm endpoint + 30-day soft-delete grace window + daily purge cron + Settings > Danger Zone UI.** Pre-fix: there was no tenant-facing path to terminate an account. The super-admin `/super-admin/api/tenants/:slug` DELETE soft-deleted via `deleteTenant()` (which already respects a 30-day grace via `archive/`) but required a platform super-admin — a tenant who wanted out had to email support. Per the project memory rule "tenant DB files are sacred — this is the ONE allowed deletion path: explicit, user-initiated," PROD59 wires up that one allowed path with maximum friction so nothing short of a fully-intentional admin action can cross the line. Post-fix: new `packages/server/src/services/tenantTermination.ts` (~360 lines) owns the three-stage state machine and the filesystem operation. Tokens live in an in-memory `Map` with a 5-minute TTL + `setInterval` reaper. Token equality uses `crypto.timingSafeEqual` on UTF-8 buffers so the slug/phrase comparisons don't leak length via timing. (a) **`POST /api/v1/admin/terminate-tenant`** mounted inside `packages/server/src/routes/admin.routes.ts` BEFORE the token-based admin-panel auth middleware AND before the multi-tenant kill-switch — uses the tenant JWT via `authMiddleware` + `req.user.role === 'admin'` gate, so it's reachable from a shop's own Settings even though the rest of `/api/v1/admin/*` is super-admin-only. Three branches on `action`: (b) **`action: 'request'`** — mints a fresh 32-byte hex token via `crypto.randomBytes(32).toString('hex')`, stores `{ slug, tenantId, adminUserId, adminUsername, adminEmail, stage: 'issued', expiresAt }` in the in-memory Map, sends a best-effort notification email to the tenant's `admin_email` (via the existing per-tenant `sendEmail(db, opts)` which reads SMTP config from `store_config`; failure does NOT block token return — if SMTP is misconfigured the caller who just authenticated still gets the token), and returns `{ token, expires_at }`. Email body explains what happened, shows the requesting IP + admin username + expiry, tells the recipient that IF they didn't initiate this they can ignore it (token auto-expires), and nudges them to rotate their password via the linked app URL. Single-tenant mode returns 400 with a clear error telling operators to remove their self-hosted install manually. (c) **`action: 'confirm'`** — caller posts `{ token, typed_slug }`, server validates the token still exists + hasn't expired + has stage `'issued'`, and `timingSafeEquals` the typed slug against the stored slug (case-sensitive). On match the token's stage advances to `'slug_confirmed'` and we return `{ stage: 'slug_confirmed' }`. Mismatch returns 400 with a generic "Typed subdomain does not match" message so attackers can't probe for existing token/slug pairs. (d) **`action: 'finalize'`** — the only branch that actually touches state. Requires (i) a valid unexpired token in stage `'slug_confirmed'`, (ii) the slug typed correctly AGAIN (defense-in-depth against token theft between step 2 and step 3), and (iii) the literal string `"DELETE ALL DATA PERMANENTLY"` as `typed_phrase`. Whitespace-sensitive, case-sensitive, no punctuation. If all three match, the token is deleted from the Map FIRST (so a retry of the same POST on client timeout cannot double-execute), then `executeTermination()` performs the soft-delete. (e) **Soft-delete pipeline**: `closeTenantDb(slug)` drops the live DB handle so Windows can rename the file; `fs.renameSync(tenantDataDir/<slug>.db, tenantDataDir/deleted/<slug>-<iso-ts>.db)` (plus WAL + SHM sidecars, best-effort); master DB `tenants` row flips to `status = 'pending_deletion'` with `deletion_scheduled_at` set to now + 30 days and `archived_db_path` set to the new location for operator visibility; a `tenant_self_terminated` row goes into `master_audit_log` with the archived path + scheduled times; Cloudflare DNS record deletion is best-effort (failure is logged but does NOT abort the flow — user's intent is already expressed and a dangling DNS record is a lesser evil than leaving the DB live); session invalidation is implicit — the `sessions` table lives inside the just-renamed file, so any outstanding access token for this tenant hits authMiddleware's session-lookup on the NEXT request and gets rejected cleanly (no server-side logout loop needed). (f) **Response shape**: `{ success: true, deletion_scheduled_at, permanent_delete_at, grace_days: 30 }` so the client has a paper trail to show the user (and save for their records). (g) **Audit log every step**: `tenant_terminate_step1_request`, `tenant_terminate_step2_confirm` (with `matched: true|false`), `tenant_terminate_step3_finalize_attempt`, `tenant_terminate_step3_finalize_rejected` (with reason), `tenant_terminate_finalized`, plus `tenant_terminate_refused_single_tenant` for single-tenant-mode refusals. Every event goes through the existing `audit(db, event, userId, ip, details)` helper in `utils/audit.ts` so AuditLogsTab picks them up automatically. (h) **Daily purge cron** in `packages/server/src/index.ts` under the existing `trackInterval(...)` block (multi-tenant mode only, lazy-imports `purgeExpiredDeletions` from the service): every hour the cron checks if the current UTC hour is 03, and if `shouldRunDaily('tenant-termination-purge', 'UTC')` returns true, calls `purgeExpiredDeletions()`. The sweeper walks `deleted/` and unlinks any `*.db`/`*.db-wal`/`*.db-shm` whose `mtime` is older than `TERMINATION_GRACE_DAYS` (30). We also kick one purge at startup so a server that was offline through a scheduled deletion catches up on boot — the "never delete earlier than scheduled" invariant holds because the cutoff is mtime-based, not tick-based. (i) **Front-end UI** — new `packages/web/src/pages/settings/DangerZoneTab.tsx` (4-step modal state machine: `intro → request → confirm_slug → confirm_phrase → done`, with a "Request Account Termination" button on the landing tab that's disabled unless `useAuthStore().user.role === 'admin'`). Each step has a dedicated sub-component. Step 4 renders the `deletion_scheduled_at` + `permanent_delete_at` timestamps from the server response so the user has a visible grace-window countdown. Wiring: `SettingsPage.tsx` got a new `'danger-zone'` tab in the Tab union, a tabs-array entry with the `AlertTriangle` icon, a TAB_KEYWORDS row for search, and a conditional `{activeTab === 'danger-zone' && <DangerZoneTab />}` in the render. `packages/web/src/api/endpoints.ts` gained `tenantTerminationApi = { request(), confirm(token, slug), finalize(token, slug, phrase) }` with typed response shapes. (j) **Verified**: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` — zero errors. `cd packages/web && npm run build` — built in 8.77s, SettingsPage chunk 362.75kB (gzip 69.84kB). Files added: `packages/server/src/services/tenantTermination.ts` (~360 lines), `packages/web/src/pages/settings/DangerZoneTab.tsx` (~400 lines). Files modified: `packages/server/src/routes/admin.routes.ts` (~110 lines: endpoint handler + bypass for existing middleware), `packages/server/src/index.ts` (+40 lines: daily purge cron), `packages/web/src/api/endpoints.ts` (+30 lines: typed API), `packages/web/src/pages/settings/SettingsPage.tsx` (+10 lines: tab wiring), `TODO.md` (migrated). Commit e0fa615.

- [x] PROD58. **Per-tenant "download all my data" capability — GDPR/CCPA JSON export endpoint + Settings UI button.** Pre-fix: there was no tenant-facing way to obtain a full data archive. The existing `/api/v1/settings-ext/export.json` only covered `store_config` (shop settings); the `/api/v1/admin/backup` path produces encrypted backups that require the server's key to read and is disabled in multi-tenant mode. GDPR Article 20 (right to data portability) and CCPA Section 1798.110 (right to know) both require the data subject to receive a copy of their personal data in a machine-readable format on request — neither of the existing endpoints satisfied that for a tenant admin. Post-fix: new `packages/server/src/routes/dataExport.routes.ts` (~300 lines) mounted at `/api/v1/data-export` via `authMiddleware` so it inherits the tenant resolver's `req.db` assignment (tenant DB in multi-tenant, global DB in single-tenant). (a) **`GET /export-all-data`** — admin-role-gated (`adminOnly` middleware inside the router throws 403 if `req.user?.role !== 'admin'`). Reads `last_data_export_at` from `store_config` as a per-tenant rate-limit checkpoint — if another export fired in the last hour the endpoint returns 429 with `Retry-After` header + a `retry_after_seconds` payload so the UI can render a countdown. On success, writes a fresh ISO timestamp to `store_config.last_data_export_at` BEFORE streaming begins (a client that intentionally disconnects early still spends the slot — protects against abuse loops). Lists every user-owned table via `SELECT name FROM sqlite_master WHERE type = 'table' AND name NOT LIKE 'sqlite_%'`, then streams the JSON envelope `{"tenant_slug":"...","exported_at":"...","version":1,"tables":{"customers":[...],"tickets":[...],...},"row_counts":{...}}` one row at a time via `res.write(JSON.stringify(row))`. Writing per-row instead of per-table keeps peak process memory bounded for large tenants (a 500k-row invoices table no longer balloons the heap before the first byte hits the wire). (b) **Sensitive-field redaction** — the `users` table's `password_hash / totp_secret / pin_hash / recovery_codes / reset_token_hash / remember_token_hash` columns are rewritten to `null` before emission via `sanitizeRow(table, row)`, and `store_config` rows whose `key` matches `SENSITIVE_CONFIG_KEYS` (BlockChyp keys, SMS provider tokens, `smtp_pass`, `tcx_password`, `stripe_secret_key`, `twilio_auth_token`) have their `value` nulled — the export is for the tenant's own GDPR/CCPA records, not for onward transmission, and handing a plaintext bearer token to whoever intercepts the JSON file on its way to the user's disk is a gift an attacker should not receive. `EXCLUDED_TABLES` drops bookkeeping tables entirely (`_migrations`, `sqlite_sequence`, `sessions`, `refresh_tokens`, `password_history`, `login_attempts`, `rate_limits`, `rate_limit_windows`, `api_key_revocations`, `admin_tokens`, `pending_2fa_challenges`, `recovery_codes_used`) because they hold short-lived auth state with no portability value. (c) **Audit log entry** — always fires at end of request (even if the stream aborted mid-flight) via `audit(db, 'data_export', userId, ip, { tenant, filename, table_count, row_counts, total_rows })`. The `data_export` event joins the existing audit-log surface so AuditLogsTab can render it. (d) **Filename** — `bizarre-crm-export-<slug>-<YYYY-MM-DD>.json`, slug-sanitized via `safeFilenameToken` (anything outside `[a-z0-9-_]` collapses to `-`, capped at 64 chars) so an exotic tenant slug cannot inject header-breaking characters. `Content-Disposition: attachment`, `Content-Type: application/json; charset=utf-8`, `Cache-Control: no-store`, `Pragma: no-cache`, `X-Robots-Tag: noindex, nofollow`. (e) **`GET /export-all-data/status`** — read-only sibling endpoint returning `{ last_export_at, next_allowed_in_seconds, allowed, rate_limit_window_seconds }` so the Settings UI can render the "last exported" timestamp + "next allowed in N min" countdown without having to try the real endpoint and catch a 429. (f) **Web UI** — `packages/web/src/pages/settings/SettingsPage.tsx`: added `DownloadAllDataSection` component at the top of the Data & Import tab (above the Factory Wipe red-border card, below the import-progress panel). Primary-orange `<Download />` button with copy "Download all my data" + subtitle explaining GDPR/CCPA scope + what secrets are stripped + the one-per-hour limit. `useQuery` polls `/data-export/export-all-data/status` every 60s so the enabled/disabled state auto-updates without reload. `useCallback`-wrapped `triggerDownload()` calls `dataExportApi.downloadAll()` with `responseType: 'blob'`, parses `Content-Disposition` to pull the server-suggested filename, materializes the Blob via `URL.createObjectURL`, clicks a hidden `<a>` to trigger the browser's save dialog, then revokes the URL. `confirm()` dialog before the download so an accidental click doesn't start a multi-megabyte archive. 429 responses come back as Blobs (because of `responseType: 'blob'`) so the error path reads the Blob back via `.text()` + `JSON.parse()` to surface the server's `message` in a toast, then re-fetches status so the countdown reflects the block. (g) **Typed client** — `packages/web/src/api/endpoints.ts` gained `dataExportApi = { status(), downloadAll() }` with a named `DataExportStatus` interface so downstream callers get autocomplete on the four response fields. Verified: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` → zero errors; `cd packages/web && npm run build` → built in 8.64s, SettingsPage chunk 350.56kB (gzip 67.33kB). Files added: `packages/server/src/routes/dataExport.routes.ts` (312 lines). Files modified: `packages/server/src/index.ts` (+8 lines: import + mount), `packages/web/src/api/endpoints.ts` (+25 lines: typed api surface), `packages/web/src/pages/settings/SettingsPage.tsx` (+118 lines: DownloadAllDataSection component + usage + import), `TODO.md` (PROD58 migrated). Commit TBD.

- [x] PROD78-79-80-81. **Public-release docs: MIT LICENSE + public README + LICENSES.md + workspace-root pointer.** Phase-10 repo-polish cluster landed as one change because the four items share a single audience (anyone cloning the repo from GitHub for the first time) and cross-reference each other (README links LICENSE + LICENSES.md; LICENSES.md notes LICENSE covers the project itself; workspace-root pointer README defers to the repo README). (a) **PROD80 — LICENSE (MIT)**: new `LICENSE` file at `bizarre-crm/` repo root, canonical MIT text, copyright line `Copyright (c) 2026 Bizarre Electronics CRM contributors`. MIT chosen over Apache-2.0 / AGPL / proprietary because: (1) repair-shop tooling has no patent-sensitivity justifying Apache-2.0's extra clauses for a solo-maintainer project, (2) AGPL's network-clause would poison any prospective managed-hosting partner who wants to run the server for a shop without being forced to redistribute their ops scripts, (3) MIT is the broadest-compatibility permissive license — every third-party dep in `LICENSES.md` (MIT, ISC, Apache-2.0, BSD) is already upstream-compatible with MIT downstream, and forking shops can drop the project into whatever downstream arrangement they need without a compatibility audit. (b) **PROD78 — public README rewrite**: `README.md` fully rewritten to lead with tagline "Open-source repair-shop CRM replacing RepairDesk." and an alpha-software disclaimer block up top (self-host at your own risk, back up tenant DBs regularly, pointer to the Restore Drill section). Architecture compressed to one paragraph (Node.js + Express + SQLite via better-sqlite3 + React 19 + Vite + TypeScript, multi-tenant with one DB file per tenant, Android Compose field app, Electron management panel, single process serves API + static + WebSocket). Setup section is a verbatim command sequence — `git clone` → `npm install` → `cp .env.example .env` + generate JWT secrets via `node -e "require('crypto').randomBytes(64).toString('hex')"` → `npm --workspace=packages/web run build` → `cd packages/server && npx tsx src/index.ts` — so a visitor can land, skim, copy-paste, and boot in order. Env vars section links directly to `.env.example` for the full comment-annotated list. Default creds block is a 3-row table (admin / admin123, PIN 1234) with a bold note that 2FA is forced on first login. Contributing section is brief and actionable (run security tests, `npm run build`, `npx tsc --noEmit` clean, update contract docs when shapes change). Kept the existing Node-25-ABI note, production TLS section, restore drill, and further-reading links because they're high-leverage for new operators. The pre-rewrite README was 582 lines of wandering prose optimized for a private internal audience ("BizarreCRM is a self-hosted repair shop system for Bizarre Electronics"); the new version is 183 lines optimized for "someone who found this on GitHub". (c) **PROD81 — LICENSES.md rewrite**: restructured as four per-workspace tables (server, web, shared, management) plus Android section + build-time-only section, each row `| Package | Version | License |` matching the requested schema. Every version string is pulled from the actual `package.json` caret ranges (`^19.0.0`, `^12.8.0`, etc.) so the file stays accurate without a manual audit. Top notice makes the "transitive deps inherit parent licenses — this file is top-level only" caveat explicit and tells operators to run `npx license-checker --summary` for the full audit. License-summary table at the top shows no GPL/AGPL/SSPL in the top-level set (sharp's LGPL-3.0 natives are dynamically linked and unmodified — operators can substitute their own libvips/glib/pango). Android deps enumerated from `packages/android/app/build.gradle.kts` (AndroidX, Compose BOM 2025.03.00, Room 2.7.0, Retrofit 2.11.0, Firebase BOM 33.8.0, Coil 3.1.0, Hilt 2.53, Vico 2.0.1, etc.) — all Apache-2.0 except net.zetetic:sqlcipher-android 4.6.1 (BSD-style). (d) **PROD79 — repo-root README**: no `README.md` existed at `C:\Users\Owner\Downloads\MY OWN CRM\` (the local workspace that wraps the `bizarre-crm/` git repo — the wrapper directory itself is not under version control, it's a local scratch folder containing audit screenshots + scratch markdowns + the actual repo). Created a one-paragraph pointer README there explaining that `bizarre-crm/` is the real source repo and redirecting all setup/architecture/license questions to `bizarre-crm/README.md`. Chose "simplified pointer" over "mirror" because the wrapper directory is ephemeral-ish (not versioned, contains local-dev noise) and maintaining two in-sync copies of the real README is maintenance debt for zero reader benefit — nobody clones the wrapper, they clone the repo. (e) **`.gitignore` fix**: the repo's aggressive `*.md` ignore rule with whitelist (lines 87-94) already permitted `README.md / TODO.md / DONETODOS.md / SECURITY.md / docs/**/*.md` but blocked the new `LICENSES.md`. - [x] SA1-1. **JWT secrets can now be rotated gracefully without invalidating every active session.** Pre-fix: every `jwt.verify(token, config.jwtSecret, ...)` and `jwt.verify(refreshToken, config.jwtRefreshSecret, ...)` used a single secret. Rotating `JWT_SECRET` meant every already-issued access + refresh token failed verification the instant the server restarted, kicking every logged-in user out of the app mid-workday. Operators therefore avoided rotating JWT secrets even when they had reason to (suspected leak, routine credential hygiene, staff offboarding with deploy-shell access) — the user-facing churn of forcing every employee to re-authenticate was worse than the perceived risk. Post-fix: new `utils/jwtSecrets.ts` module exposes `verifyJwtWithRotation(token, 'access'|'refresh', options)` which tries the current secret first and falls back to the optional `JWT_SECRET_PREVIOUS` / `JWT_REFRESH_SECRET_PREVIOUS` secret ONLY on signature-verification failure (`JsonWebTokenError` whose `.name === 'JsonWebTokenError'`). TokenExpiredError / NotBeforeError are NOT rescued by the fallback — expired tokens should stay expired regardless of which key signed them. Signing always uses the current secret; the previous secret is verify-only so leaving it set forever by accident cannot produce new tokens signed with it. (a) **`config.ts`** — added `jwtSecretPrevious` + `jwtRefreshSecretPrevious` IIFE accessors that read `JWT_SECRET_PREVIOUS` / `JWT_REFRESH_SECRET_PREVIOUS` from env, return `undefined` when unset, and refuse to load obviously-insecure placeholders (the well-known `change-me-*` / `dev-*-change-me` strings, plus any value shorter than 32 chars) with a warning so an operator who accidentally pastes a dev value into the previous slot doesn't silently widen the verification surface. (b) **`middleware/auth.ts`** — `authMiddleware`'s `jwt.verify(token, config.jwtSecret, ...)` now routes through `verifyJwtWithRotation(token, 'access', ...)`. Import of `jwt` was kept for `JsonWebTokenError`-shape checks elsewhere in the file but `jwt.verify` no longer appears here. (c) **`ws/server.ts`** — websocket auth uses the same rotation-aware verifier so a token that passes HTTP auth also passes WS auth (symmetric behavior is required — otherwise a rotation would silently break realtime updates). `config` import became unused after the refactor and was removed. (d) **`routes/auth.routes.ts`** — the `POST /refresh` handler's refresh-token verify uses `verifyJwtWithRotation(refreshToken, 'refresh', ...)`. Access-token signing + refresh-token signing both untouched: they always use the current secret. (e) **`routes/super-admin.routes.ts`** — new `POST /rotate-jwt-secret` endpoint gated by the existing `superAdminAuth` middleware. Accepts `{ purpose: 'access' | 'refresh' | 'both' }` (default `'both'`), generates fresh 64-byte hex secret(s) via `generateJwtSecret()`, returns them in the response body along with a step-by-step instructions array. Deliberately does NOT write to process.env — Node env mutations don't propagate to child workers, and in real deploys the env is owned by systemd / PM2 / Docker / Kubernetes secrets / a vault. The endpoint records `super_admin_rotate_jwt_secret` in `master_audit_log` with the purpose + a sanity-check hex-char count but never the secret value itself. (f) **`utils/startupValidation.ts`** — calls new `warnIfPreviousSecretsSet()` helper which emits a 5-line boot warning whenever either `_PREVIOUS` env is still set, pointing to `docs/operator-guide.md` for the removal procedure. This nag fires on every restart until operators remove the vars, so stale rotation state is visible. (g) **`.env.example`** — documents `JWT_SECRET_PREVIOUS` + `JWT_REFRESH_SECRET_PREVIOUS` with the rotation workflow in a comment. (h) **`docs/operator-guide.md`** — new "JWT Secret Rotation" section before "Backups": 5-step graceful procedure (generate → move old to _PREVIOUS → restart → wait ~90 min → remove _PREVIOUS → restart), explanation of why sign always uses current while verify accepts both, pointer to the super-admin rotation endpoint for multi-tenant setups, and note that the app never writes to env itself. (i) **`scripts/test-jwt-rotation.mjs`** — 6 unit tests covering the critical paths: current-secret token verifies, previous-secret token verifies during rotation window, nonsense-secret token fails, rotation is opt-in (no previous = old tokens reject), expired tokens throw `TokenExpiredError` not rescued by fallback, and new tokens are always signed HS256 regardless of rotation state. Reconstructs the verifier in plain JS so the test is hermetic and doesn't drag in `config.ts`'s `process.exit` side-effects. Verified with `cd packages/server && node scripts/test-jwt-rotation.mjs` → **6 passed, 0 failed**. TypeScript clean: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` — no errors. Behavioural diff for operators who DON'T rotate: exactly zero — `JWT_SECRET_PREVIOUS` defaults to undefined, the fallback branch is never taken, and every verify goes through `jwt.verify(token, config.jwtSecret, options)` via a one-line wrapper. Commit aa65ce5.

- [x] SA7-1. **Blocking sleep loops now have persistent per-job checkpoints so a mid-import crash can resume instead of replaying the whole queue.** Pre-fix: `packages/server/src/scripts/reimport-notes.ts` and `packages/server/src/services/repairDeskImport.ts#importTicketNotesAndHistory` walked the `import_id_map` for every imported RepairDesk ticket with a per-record `await sleep(200)` between fetches; `packages/server/src/services/myRepairAppImport.ts` and `packages/server/src/services/repairShoprImport.ts` did the same at page granularity. The loop cursor was a stack-local `processed` counter — a Node crash, OOM kill, or operator Ctrl-C lost it entirely and the only recovery path was "rerun from 0", which replays thousands of external API requests and risks double-writes against the remote catalog. Post-fix: new migration `106_import_job_state.sql` adds the `import_job_state(job_id TEXT PK, step INT, total INT, last_processed_id TEXT, status, last_error, started_at, updated_at)` table with indexes on `status` and `updated_at`. New helper module `packages/server/src/services/importJobState.ts` exposes `buildJobId(source, entity, tenantSlug)` for a stable key format, `resumeJobState(db, jobId, { total, startFresh })` to claim/create the row, `parseResumeFlags(argv)` for shared CLI parsing, plus a handle object with `shouldSkip(recordId, rowIndex) / checkpoint({ step, lastProcessedId }) / markRunning / markPaused / complete / fail`. The critical invariant: `checkpoint()` is called from INSIDE the same `db.transaction(() => { ... })` that performs the row writes, so progress and writes commit or roll back together — a crash mid-batch never leaves the cursor ahead of the data (or vice versa). `shouldSkip()` supports both cursor-based (source id) and index-based (row position) comparison; numeric ids use `<=` ordering so a resume after ticket N skips everything N and earlier. Patched call sites: (a) **`scripts/reimport-notes.ts`** — added `import { buildJobId, resumeJobState, parseResumeFlags, type ResumeCliFlags }`, extended `CliArgs` with `ResumeCliFlags`, rewrote the argv parser to also accept `--resume` / `--start-fresh` (mutually exclusive; default is start-fresh to preserve "re-run from 0" muscle memory). The main loop now iterates by index so `shouldSkip(rdId, idx)` can short-circuit. Each ticket's notes + history INSERTs + `jobState.checkpoint({ step, lastProcessedId: rdId })` all live inside one `db.transaction(() => { ... })()`. Skip paths (already-has-notes, non-429 HTTP error, `json.success === false`) still checkpoint so a resume doesn't revisit them; 429 rate-limit and network errors intentionally DON'T checkpoint so the same ticket is retried on restart. Fatal errors in the outer main() catch call `jobState.fail(msg)` best-effort. (b) **`services/repairDeskImport.ts#importTicketNotesAndHistory`** — same pattern for the in-process import path: takes an optional `{ startFresh }` opt (defaults to false for in-process continuity), builds `buildJobId('repairdesk', 'ticket-notes-history', tenantSlug)`, checkpoints inside the notes+history transaction, respects cancelFlags via `jobState.markPaused()`, and advances `jobState.complete(processed)` on clean exit. `cancelFlags` (existing tenant-scoped Ctrl-C signal) now properly marks the row paused instead of leaving it in 'running' forever. (c) **`scripts/full-import.ts`** — usage docs updated to mention the forwarded `--resume` / `--start-fresh` flags; no code change needed because it already spawns reimport-notes via `await import('./reimport-notes.js')` which inherits process.argv. Shared CLI parser: `parseResumeFlags(argv)` throws if both flags are passed, defaults to `startFresh: true` if neither (conservative — matches original behavior), and lives in importJobState.ts so future import scripts pick it up for free. Out of scope for this patch (no data-write loops to checkpoint — these are page-fetch-only loops that feed the *already-transactional* entity-import batches, which have their own `import_id_map` idempotence via `findMapping` lookups): the top-level page loops in `RdApiClient.fetchAllPages` / `RsApiClient.fetchAllPages` / `MraApiClient.fetchInventoryPages`. Those already resume correctly because `insertMapping.run(runId, entity, rdId, localId)` is called inside the per-batch transaction and `findMapping` skips records that already have a row — the import_id_map itself IS their checkpoint. Adding a second checkpoint for them would be redundant and would serialize extra UPDATEs against a hot table. Verified with `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` — exit code 0, zero errors. Migration file: `packages/server/src/db/migrations/106_import_job_state.sql` (55 lines, two indexes). Files added: `services/importJobState.ts` (248 lines). Files modified: `scripts/reimport-notes.ts` (~60 lines diff), `scripts/full-import.ts` (docstring-only), `services/repairDeskImport.ts` (~50 lines diff in `importTicketNotesAndHistory`). Commit 1f50f6e.

- [x] SA10-1. **Lingering `as any` casts at the webhook / invoice event-broadcast boundary removed — three call sites now use narrowed types.** Pre-fix: `packages/server/src/routes/invoices.routes.ts:318` (`fireWebhook(db, 'invoice_created', { invoice_id, order_id: (invoice as any)?.order_id })`) and `packages/server/src/routes/tickets.routes.ts:1149` + `:2095` carried `(<row> as any)?.order_id` escape-hatch casts. Root cause: `getInvoiceDetail` / `getFullTicketAsync` spread `adb.get<any>(...)` rows into their return value, so the detail-row types were loose `any`/`AnyRow = Record<string, any>` shapes that Typescript couldn't verify; the cast at the broadcast boundary silenced the "possibly undefined" lint without actually answering the question "does this row really have an `order_id` string?". Post-fix: (a) `invoices.routes.ts` — the POST `/invoices` handler ALREADY computed the invoice `orderId` locally earlier in the handler (`const orderId = formatInvoiceOrderId(nextSeq)` at line 226), and that's the literal value we INSERT into `invoices.order_id`. The webhook fire-site now uses that local variable directly — same value, zero cast. (b) `tickets.routes.ts:1149` — symmetric fix; the POST handler has `const orderId = formatTicketOrderId(ticketSeq)` in scope at line 972 (well before the line-1149 webhook fire-site), so the `ticket_created` webhook now passes `orderId` directly instead of reading it back off `ticket` via a cast. (c) `tickets.routes.ts:2095` — the PATCH `/tickets/:id/status` handler does NOT have a local `orderId` available (it receives the ticket id on the URL and only fetches the full ticket via `getFullTicketAsync` afterward). Replaced the `(ticket as any)?.order_id` with a typed-narrowing pattern: `const ticketOrderId = ticket && typeof (ticket as { order_id?: unknown }).order_id === 'string' ? (ticket as { order_id: string }).order_id : undefined`. The `{ order_id?: unknown }` shape lets us ask the question, `typeof === 'string'` actually answers it, and the narrowed `{ order_id: string }` accessor is safe because the guard just proved the shape. Preserves the identical null/undefined fallback semantics the original optional-chain produced (if `ticket` is null, or `order_id` is missing / non-string, the webhook body receives `undefined` — exactly what the old `(ticket as any)?.order_id` would have yielded). Behavioural diff: zero. Every webhook payload is byte-for-byte identical to before; only the type-checker's view of the code changed. Verified with `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` — exit code 0, zero errors. Files touched: `routes/invoices.routes.ts` (+5/-1), `routes/tickets.routes.ts` (+12/-2). Commit 6f0b376.

- [x] SA8-1. **Deep link validation — verified non-applicable after a full cross-package sweep.** The audit finding asserted that "the Electron app now implements a per-user installation without UAC, but the `setup` URL handlers lack strict deep-link origin validation, allowing potential arbitrary custom protocol abuse." After grepping `packages/management/` and the packaged `dashboard/` output for every Electron API that can surface a custom-scheme URL to the main process — `app.setAsDefaultProtocolClient`, `protocol.register*`, `protocol.handle`, `registerSchemesAsPrivileged`, `app.on('open-url', …)` (macOS), `app.on('second-instance', …)` (Windows/Linux), `app.requestSingleInstanceLock()`, and `process.argv` parsing for a custom scheme — the result is zero occurrences in source. The management app is NOT registered as a custom URL-scheme handler with the OS, does not take a single-instance lock, has no `open-url` / `second-instance` listener, and performs no `process.argv` scanning for `bizarrecrm://`-style URIs. The audit's phrase "`setup` URL handlers" appears to conflate the `management:setup` IPC channel (the initial admin-user bootstrap flow in `packages/management/src/main/ipc/management-api.ts:254`, which accepts `username` + `password` arguments and POSTs to `/api/v1/management/setup` — no URL involved) with a custom deep-link route that does not exist. The only URL parsing performed by the main process is **outbound-gating**: `isAllowedRendererUrl()` in `packages/management/src/main/window.ts:42-58` (allows only `file://` + the Vite dev-server origin for in-place navigation via `will-navigate`), the `setWindowOpenHandler` block at `window.ts:130-142` (passes window-open targets to `shell.openExternal` only when `protocol === 'http:' | 'https:'`), and `isSafeLocalUrl()` in `packages/management/src/main/ipc/system-info.ts:23-35` (gates `system:open-external` to loopback `http(s)` hosts only). All three are defensive checks that reject foreign/hostile URLs the renderer might hand *out* to the OS — the opposite threat direction from the one SA8-1 describes. The Android app and the iOS app DO register `bizarrecrm://` schemes (`packages/android/app/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml:68`, `ios/App/DeepLinkRouter.swift:23`, `ios/scripts/write-info-plist.sh:132`), and both already gate handoff with scheme-equality checks + route whitelists (`MainActivity.kt:196` `data.scheme != "bizarrecrm"` + `resolveDeepLink()` whitelist at `MainActivity.kt:259`; `DeepLinkRouter.swift:23` scheme guard) — those are covered by AND-20260414-H1/H2 and the iOS-side `DeepLinkRouter` enum allow-list, not by SA8-1 which is scoped to the Electron desktop app. Closing with no code change. If a future release adds a `bizarrecrm-management://` protocol client, the implementation must register via `app.setAsDefaultProtocolClient`, take a single-instance lock, parse the deep-link via `new URL(raw)` (never `raw.startsWith`), enforce `protocol === 'bizarrecrm-management:'` exactly, whitelist the `hostname` against a closed set of verbs (e.g. `login-token`, `open-ticket`), reject any URL with embedded credentials (`parsed.username || parsed.password`) or non-ASCII/control-char query values, cap total URL length at 2048 chars, and reject unrecognized verbs with a `console.warn` + renderer toast rather than silently falling through. That checklist is recorded here as the spec for whoever opens that door; until then there is nothing to patch and no unit test to write (the deep-link path does not exist in the management package, and scaffolding a test harness purely to cover an absent feature would be noise). Verified via repeat `grep -ri 'setAsDefaultProtocolClient|open-url|second-instance|requestSingleInstanceLock' packages/management/ dashboard/` — 0 hits in source; only prose mentions of `bizarrecrm://` appear in `docs/howtoIOS.md`, `ios/App/*.swift`, and `packages/android/**`, none of which live in the Electron app.

- [x] AUD-20260414-H3. **`/pos/checkout-with-ticket` now executes all ticket/invoice/payment writes as one atomic transaction — partial-failure orphan rows eliminated.** Pre-fix: the route ran ~15 independent `await adb.run(...)` calls for the full checkout sequence (tickets INSERT → ticket_devices INSERTs → ticket_device_parts INSERTs → ticket totals UPDATE → ticket_history INSERT → invoice INSERT/UPDATE → invoice_line_items DELETE+INSERT → tickets.invoice_id UPDATE → payments INSERTs → pos_transactions INSERT → store_credits UPDATE/INSERT → store_credit_transactions INSERT → inventory_items stock-decrement UPDATE → stock_movements INSERT → tickets.status_id close UPDATE → ticket_history status_change INSERT). An existing batched `paymentTxQueries` block only covered steps 5e onward; everything before it wrote independently. Any mid-sequence failure — a stock race triggering 409, a status lookup returning null, a connection drop, a FK violation — left orphan tickets, $0 invoices, zero-line invoices, or payments pointing at half-closed tickets that required manual reconciliation. The route's own inline comment at `pos.routes.ts:1508-1511` explicitly acknowledged the gap: "A full atomic wrapping transaction for this endpoint is out of scope". Post-fix: split the handler into preflight + atomic-write + post-commit phases. **Preflight phase (async reads, no writes)**: resolves customer + tax class + membership + referral config + warranty defaults (consolidated from 2*N SELECTs per device into one SELECT for the default row), builds a `PreparedDevice[]` / `PreparedPart[]` / `PreparedProductLine[]` plan with every write parameter pre-computed, allocates `ticketOrderId` + `invoiceOrderId` upfront via `allocateCounter` so subqueries can resolve FKs during the batch, looks up `closedStatusId` + existing store_credits row + existing invoice — ALL reads live here. **Atomic-write phase**: every INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE gets pushed into a single `TxQuery[]` and fired through `adb.transaction(txQueries)` in one call. Cross-table FKs inside the batch use order_id as a natural key (`(SELECT id FROM tickets WHERE order_id = ?)`, `(SELECT id FROM invoices WHERE order_id = ?)`) to avoid threading row-ids through async boundaries; parts-to-device FK uses `(SELECT MAX(id) FROM ticket_devices WHERE ticket_id = …)` — deterministic because the queue interleaves device, all its parts, next device, all its parts, so MAX is always the just-inserted row for the current device. Stock decrements keep their `expectChanges: true` guard → any shortage throws `E_EXPECT_CHANGES` inside better-sqlite3's `db.transaction(...)` callback, rolling back everything. The outer `try/catch` around `adb.transaction(...)` calls `refundTierReservation()` on any throw so the tenant_usage slot is freed on failure, then maps guarded-update failures to 409 Conflict. **Post-commit phase (best-effort side-effects)**: discount audit log, invoice/ticket row re-fetch for response envelope, WS `TICKET_CREATED` broadcast, in-app notifications — intentionally outside the txn so a logging/email failure never undoes a completed sale. Payment gateway rollback is not needed here because BlockChyp/Stripe calls live in a separate `blockchyp.routes.ts` endpoint; the client passes a pre-authorized token + reference + transaction_id that this route just records. If future gateway integration inlines the charge here, the comment at the top of the handler documents the pattern: "charge card first, get token, open txn, insert rows; on rollback issue refund + alert operator". New integration test fixture `packages/server/scripts/test-pos-checkout-atomic.mjs` replicates the exact TxQuery[] pattern against a real tenant DB (accepts `DB_PATH=data/tenants/<slug>.db` env var), runs two scenarios: (1) forces a stock-race E_EXPECT_CHANGES mid-batch and verifies tickets/invoices/invoice_line_items/payments/pos_transactions/in_stock counts are ALL unchanged from baseline, plus the specific ticket+invoice order_ids do NOT exist — catches regressions that break the rollback; (2) a sanity-check happy path that writes + rolls back via cleanup deletions so the test is idempotent. Verified with `DB_PATH=data/tenants/bizarreelectronics.db node scripts/test-pos-checkout-atomic.mjs` — **15 passed, 0 failed**. TypeScript clean: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` — no errors. Transaction boundary: `await adb.transaction(txQueries)` at `pos.routes.ts:1887` is the single commit point; every write lands inside it. Rollback path: better-sqlite3's synchronous `db.transaction(() => {...})` wrapper in `db-worker.mjs:122-140` ensures any throw (including tagged `E_EXPECT_CHANGES` from the stock guard) rolls the full batch; the outer `try/catch` in the route maps guarded failures to HTTP 409 and always refunds the tier reservation before re-throwing. No external gateway rollback needed (payment reference is already a post-authorization token).

- [x] AUD-20260414-M4. **Android SQLCipher rollout now has a one-shot upgrade path for pre-encryption plaintext databases.** Pre-fix: `packages/android/app/src/main/java/com/bizarreelectronics/crm/di/DatabaseModule.kt:35-43` documented the open gap — builds that shipped before the SQLCipher rollout stored Room as a plaintext SQLite file at `context.getDatabasePath("bizarre_crm.db")`. After the upgrade, Room opens that same file through `net.zetetic.database.sqlcipher.SupportOpenHelperFactory` and fails hard with "file is not a database" because SQLCipher expects a ciphertext header it can decrypt; every pre-upgrade user would hit an app-start crash before they could sync or log out. Post-fix: new `PlaintextToEncryptedMigrator` under `data/local/db/` runs exactly once per install before Room is wired up, guarded by a `sqlcipher_migration_v1_done` boolean in a dedicated plain `SharedPreferences` file (`sqlcipher_migration_prefs`). (a) **Detection path** — the migrator first checks the flag in O(1); then stats `bizarre_crm.db`. No file = fresh install → mark done + return (Room will create an encrypted DB from scratch). File present = try to open it as plaintext with the system `android.database.sqlite.SQLiteDatabase.openDatabase(path, null, OPEN_READONLY)` — if the open succeeds the file is legitimately plaintext; if it throws `SQLiteException` ("file is not a database") the header is already SQLCipher-encrypted → mark done + return (Room takes over). Unexpected throws are conservatively treated as "don't touch". (b) **Export path** — opens the plaintext file again via SQLCipher's `net.zetetic.database.sqlcipher.SQLiteDatabase.openDatabase(path, "" /* empty key */, null, OPEN_READWRITE, null /* hook */)` (empty key bypasses SQLCipher's encryption layer; the file reads as standard SQLite), then runs the canonical recipe `ATTACH DATABASE '<stagingPath>' AS encrypted KEY "x'<hex>'"` + `SELECT sqlcipher_export('encrypted')` + `DETACH DATABASE encrypted`. The `KEY "x'<hex>'"` literal tells SQLCipher the 64-char hex payload is a raw encryption key (no PBKDF2 derivation) which matches how `DatabaseModule` already feeds the key to Room. `rawQuery(...).use { c -> c.moveToFirst() }` is used instead of `execSQL` so the pragma-style SELECT actually executes. ATTACH uses embedded literals (not `?` bind params) with a defensive `require(!path.contains('\''))` guard because SQLite's ATTACH syntax historically varies on parameter-binding support and the path comes from the app's own trusted `getDatabasePath`. (c) **Atomic swap** — on successful export, the plaintext file is renamed to `bizarre_crm.legacy.db` (quarantined, intentionally NOT deleted as a safety net if something downstream corrupts the new DB), and the encrypted staging file `bizarre_crm.db.enc.tmp` is renamed into place as `bizarre_crm.db`. The three SQLite sidecars (`-journal`, `-wal`, `-shm`) are moved alongside each rename so the final file set is consistent — renaming only the main file would leave a stale journal pointing at the old header and confuse SQLite on the next open. Stale staging artifacts from a crashed previous attempt are purged before the export runs, so a partial migration resumes cleanly. (d) **Failure handling** — any throw during export (disk full, `sqlcipher_export` failure, rename failure) rolls back by deleting the staging file + sidecars and raising a typed `PlaintextToEncryptedMigrator.MigrationFailedException("Unable to upgrade local database to encrypted storage... Free some storage and relaunch the app.", cause)`. Critically the original plaintext file is untouched on any failure path, so the user's data is never lost; the exception bubbles out of `DatabaseModule.provideDatabase` before Room even touches the file, giving the app a chance to surface a readable error instead of a "file is not a database" SIGSEGV from deep inside SQLite. (e) **Flag key**: `sqlcipher_migration_v1_done` lives in the non-encrypted prefs file `sqlcipher_migration_prefs` (the flag carries no secrets; keeping it out of `EncryptedSharedPreferences` avoids a master-key dependency on the migration gate itself, which would be chicken-and-egg if Keystore was the source of a future similar bug). (f) **Wiring**: `DatabaseModule.provideDatabase` now calls `PlaintextToEncryptedMigrator.migrateIfNeeded(context, passphrase)` between `DatabasePassphrase.loadOrCreate(context)` and `SupportOpenHelperFactory(passphraseBytes)`. The SQLCipher native library is already loaded by `BizarreCrmApp.onCreate` via `System.loadLibrary("sqlcipher")`, which runs before Hilt resolves the `@Singleton` DB module, so the SQLCipher build of SQLite is available by the time the migrator opens its connection. The legacy KDoc warning at lines 35-43 was rewritten to point at the new migrator + describe the fresh/partial/upgraded paths + the `sqlcipher_migration_v1_done` flag. (g) **Logcat observability**: every successful migration writes `Log.i("PlaintextToEncryptedMigrator", "Migrated plaintext DB to SQLCipher")`; fresh-install short-circuit + already-encrypted short-circuit each emit their own `Log.i` with the reason; export failures log `Log.e` with the throwable cause before rolling back. Verified with `cd packages/android && JAVA_HOME='/c/Program Files/Android/Android Studio/jbr' ./gradlew clean :app:compileDebugKotlin` — BUILD SUCCESSFUL in 34s (pre-existing deprecation warnings only: `Icons.Filled.Chat` / `Icons.Filled.ArrowBack` / `Modifier.menuAnchor()` / `InventoryItemEntity.costPrice|retailPrice` / `NetworkMonitor.allNetworks` / Gson `setLenient` — none introduced by this change). Files added: `PlaintextToEncryptedMigrator.kt` (303 lines); files modified: `DatabaseModule.kt` (imports + migrator call + KDoc rewrite, ~20 lines). Commit da4ba4d.

- [x] AUD-20260414-M2. **Electron management root resolution now compares candidate roots against the resolved trusted anchor instead of the filesystem drive root.** Pre-fix: `packages/management/src/main/ipc/management-api.ts:108` and `packages/management/src/main/ipc/service-control.ts:80` walked up to six levels from `app.getAppPath()` / `process.resourcesPath` looking for any one of `ecosystem.config.js` / `install.bat` / `setup.bat`, then verified the candidate via `isPathUnder(dir, path.parse(anchorRoot).root)` — `path.parse(X).root` on Windows resolves to the drive letter (`C:\`), so the containment check accepted *any* directory on the same drive as the Electron binary. A marker-bearing ancestor anywhere on disk (`C:\temp\`, `C:\Users\Public\`, a rogue sibling repo) would be accepted as the CRM project root, which lets a misplaced install silently run from arbitrary locations and widens the blast radius for `update.bat` / `taskkill` / `sc stop` redirection on compromised hosts. Post-fix: both resolvers dropped the filesystem walk entirely in favor of deterministic, layout-specific candidates anchored to the actual Electron trust anchors. (a) **`resolveTrustedProjectRoot()` in `management-api.ts`**: when `app.isPackaged === true`, the only accepted root is `<process.resourcesPath>/crm-source` (populated by `electron-builder.yml` `extraResources` — verified the config block at lines 88-113 lists the source tree exactly matching this path). If `process.resourcesPath` is missing/inaccessible or `crm-source` doesn't exist, the resolver `throw`s a clear `Installation integrity check failed — reinstall required (...)` error so a tampered install fails loudly at the first IPC call rather than silently redirecting. When `app.isPackaged === false` (dev), the root is `path.resolve(app.getAppPath(), '..', '..')` (monorepo layout: `app.getAppPath()` returns `<repo>/packages/management`, so `../../` is the repo root) — no walking, one candidate, one check. Both branches now require the FULL marker set via `hasProjectRootMarkers(dir)`: `package.json` + `packages/server/package.json` (core) AND at least one of `ecosystem.config.js` / `install.bat` / `setup.bat` (aux). Sibling-only markers (e.g. a `setup.bat` that exists without the `packages/server/` tree) are rejected. (b) **`service-control.ts`** follows the same algorithm with an identical `hasFullProjectRootMarkers(dir)` gate that composes over the existing `isProjectRoot(dir)` helper. Kept in-file rather than shared so the two modules remain decoupled at the source level (as the pre-existing comment noted). (c) **Integrity-failure handling at call sites**: `registerManagementIpc()` wraps the startup call in try/catch and logs a `[Dashboard] Installation integrity check failed during IPC init:` error — the dashboard still boots so the renderer can surface a human-readable error, but the `.env` port-discovery and `update.bat` / rollback paths all return structured `INSTALLATION_INTEGRITY_FAILED` responses when the throw fires at use-time. `service-control.ts.getProjectRoot()` is now a best-effort wrapper that catches the throw, logs to `[ServiceControl]`, and returns null — most of its callers use the root as an optional `cwd` hint for pm2 / sc, and degrading to null lets those commands fall back to their default cwd (the strict check is in `startDirectServer()` which surfaces a readable error). (d) **Belt-and-braces `.env` containment check**: the `envPath` resolution in `registerManagementIpc()` is now `path.resolve(path.join(root, '.env'))` + an explicit `isPathUnder(envPath, root)` assertion before the `fs.readFileSync` — if a symlink or future refactor ever resolves outside the trusted root we refuse to read it. (e) **`update.bat` containment check preserved** — the existing `isPathUnder(updateBat, root)` guard at the `perform-update` handler still applies and now rides on top of the stricter anchor, so the combined check is (updateBat inside root) AND (root inside trusted anchor). Verified with `cd packages/management && npm run build:main && npm run build:preload` — both TypeScript projects compile clean with zero errors. Files patched: `packages/management/src/main/ipc/management-api.ts` (~100 lines changed — replaced `resolveTrustedProjectRoot`, added `hasProjectRootMarkers` helper, wrapped IPC init + perform-update + rollback-update in try/catch, added envPath containment assertion); `packages/management/src/main/ipc/service-control.ts` (~60 lines changed — replaced `resolveTrustedProjectRoot`, added `hasFullProjectRootMarkers` helper, converted `getProjectRoot` to swallow throws). Out of scope (per the audit's suggested-fix third bullet): unit tests for sibling/ancestor marker rejection — the management package has no existing jest/vitest setup and scaffolding one sits outside a single audit item's remit; flagged in the commit body for a follow-up.

- [x] D4-1. **Laggy State Transitions** — added `onMutate` optimistic cache updates to the four hot-path ticket mutations so the UI reflects the user's action in the same frame instead of waiting ~200-400ms for the server round-trip + React Query invalidate. Pre-fix: `KanbanBoard.tsx` / `TicketDetailPage.tsx` / `TicketNotes.tsx` / `TicketSidebar.tsx` all relied on `onSuccess` → `invalidateQueries` to refresh the UI, which meant drag/drop + status-pill clicks + note Save + assignee swap each visibly lagged behind the pointer release by a full network round-trip; power users perceived the CRM as sluggish compared to instantaneous modern apps. Post-fix: every touched mutation follows the same four-callback pattern — (i) `onMutate` cancels in-flight queries for the affected key so a stale refetch doesn't race the optimistic write, snapshots the current cache via `getQueryData`, applies the optimistic mutation via `setQueryData`, and returns the snapshot in the context object, (ii) `onError` restores the snapshot from context and surfaces an error toast, (iii) `onSuccess` shows the success toast / fires the undo-window toast (in status-change flows), (iv) `onSettled` fires the existing invalidate so the cache eventually reconciles against server state. Specific changes: (a) **`pages/tickets/KanbanBoard.tsx`** — `statusMutation` on drag-end now deep-clones the cached `['tickets-kanban']` response, walks every column to `splice()` the moved ticket out of its source column, rewrites `status_id` on the moved entry, and `unshift()`es it into the target column so the card snaps across the board in the same frame as the drop. Rollback on error restores the full column layout. (b) **`pages/tickets/TicketDetailPage.tsx`** — `changeStatusMut` optimistically overwrites `status_id` + the resolved `status` object on the `['ticket', ticketId]` cache so the status pill at the header flips instantly; the undo-toast path keeps working because we now thread `prevStatusId` through the context snapshot instead of reading `ticket?.status_id` post-invalidation (which would already be the new value). Invalidation was moved from `onSuccess` to `onSettled` so the optimistic state renders while the refetch is in flight. (c) **`pages/tickets/TicketNotes.tsx`** — `addNoteMut` builds a fully-typed `TicketNote` placeholder (negative `id` from `-Date.now()` so it can't collide with a real note, `ticket_device_id: null`, `parent_id: null`, type narrowed to the `'internal' | 'diagnostic' | 'email'` shape the type demands, `user` object sourced from `useAuthStore` so the avatar/initials render correctly) and `unshift`es it into the cached ticket's `notes` array; also eagerly calls `clearNoteDraft()` during `onMutate` so the textarea resets the moment the user clicks Save rather than after the server acknowledges. Rollback restores the prior notes list. (d) **`pages/tickets/TicketSidebar.tsx`** — `assignMut` rewrites `assigned_to` + `assigned_user` on the cached `['ticket', ticketId]` payload, sourcing the full employee object (`id / first_name / last_name / avatar_url`) from the passed-in `employees` prop so the sidebar card renders the new tech's name without a refetch. Null userId (unassign) sets `assigned_user = null` cleanly. Also added a local `useQueryClient()` call at this component's scope since assign was previously the only mutation in the function body that didn't need it. Out of scope / intentionally untouched: `TicketListPage.tsx` `changeStatusMut` + `pinMut` already carry the onMutate pattern from a prior pass — confirmed both follow the same four-callback shape and left as-is. Delete / void flows are owned by the D4-5 `useUndoableAction` hook which already implements the optimistic-hide path on its own schedule; rewriting them to use `onMutate` would fight the 5-second undo window. Verified with `cd packages/web && npm run build` — built in 8.65s, zero TS errors, TicketDetailPage chunk ~130.80kB (gzip 28.89kB) unchanged in magnitude. Commit 25c4790.

- [x] D4-5. **No Recoverable Destructive Actions** — added a reusable 5-second undo window to every destructive action in the web CRM. New hook `packages/web/src/hooks/useUndoableAction.tsx` owns the pattern: on `trigger(args)` it shows a `react-hot-toast` toast with an "Undo" button, starts a 5000ms timer, and only fires the real action when the timer elapses. If the user clicks Undo the timer is cleared, the toast dismisses, and an optional `onUndo` callback restores UI state; if the component unmounts while the window is open the action fires immediately so intent is never silently dropped; if the real action throws after firing, the error toast surfaces and `onUndo` reverts the optimistic state. Rationale for the delayed-server-call approach (over an undo-after-delete with a revert endpoint): no new API surface needed, and even a failed server call leaves the DB untouched instead of relying on soft-delete + restore round-trips. Wired into six call sites: (1) `pages/customers/CustomerListPage.tsx` — `customerApi.delete` routes through `scheduleCustomerDelete()` which optimistically strips the row from every cached `['customers']` React Query page via `queryClient.setQueriesData` then schedules the real DELETE; Undo invalidates to restore. (2) `pages/invoices/InvoiceDetailPage.tsx` — `invoiceApi.void` routes through `scheduleVoidInvoice()` which flips the cached invoice's `status` to `'void'` for instant UI feedback then schedules the real POST; Undo invalidates. (3) `pages/tickets/TicketListPage.tsx` — `ticketApi.delete` routes through `scheduleTicketDelete(id, label)` which filters the row out of the tickets cache (handles both `data.data.tickets` and `data.tickets` response shapes) and schedules; ticket status-change undo was already in place from prior work and remains unchanged. (4) `pages/tickets/TicketDetailPage.tsx` — `ticketApi.delete` routes through `scheduleTicketDelete()` which strips cached list rows, fires the undoable action, and immediately `navigate('/tickets')` so the user sees the result; Undo invalidates both the list and detail caches. (5) `pages/leads/LeadListPage.tsx` — `leadApi.delete` routes through `scheduleLeadDelete(id, name)` (same optimistic-filter + schedule pattern). (6) `pages/leads/LeadDetailPage.tsx` — status changes route through `scheduleStatusChange(to, from)` which optimistically mutates the cached `['lead', id]` status field and schedules `leadApi.update(id, { status })`; the existing `updateMut` (used for notes, lost-reason, etc.) is untouched so non-status updates remain immediate. Lost-reason modal still calls `updateMut.mutate` directly — lost requires a structured reason so treating it as a plain status tap with 5s-undo would be wrong UX. Verified with `cd packages/web && npm run build` — built in 9.49s, `useUndoableAction-*.js` chunk emitted at 2.07kB (0.89kB gzip), no TS errors. Out of scope (existing behavior preserved): the bulk delete path (`bulkMut` in TicketListPage) and the merge-ticket flow — bulk ops already show a confirmation dialog with typed-match confirmation and merge is irreversible by design. Ticket status-change undo on `TicketListPage.tsx` / `TicketDetailPage.tsx` kept as-is (reverse-mutation pattern — server call already fires, Undo fires the inverse call); rewriting them to the delayed-call pattern would churn working code for no user-visible benefit.

- [x] AUD-20260414-M5. **Android dead-letter sync failures now have a user-facing recovery path.** Pre-fix: `SyncQueueDao.kt` already exposed `observeDeadLetterEntries()` + `getDeadLetterCount()` + `resurrectDeadLetter(id)` (added in a prior audit pass for R9/N8) but nothing in the UI layer consumed them — the DAO even carried a `TODO(UI): surface dead-letter entries in a "Failed Syncs" settings screen` block at line 21-22, and `SyncStatusBadge.kt` only rendered pending/syncing/synced states so dead-lettered rows were invisible to the technician. Post-fix: (a) **DAO** — added `countDeadLetter(): Int` suspend variant alongside the existing Flow counter for one-shot snapshot use; replaced the `TODO(UI)` block with a pointer to the new screen + manager entry point. (b) **SyncManager** — added `retryDeadLetter(id: Long)` public entry point that delegates to `syncQueueDao.resurrectDeadLetter(id)` (resets status to `pending` + zeroes retries) then kicks an opportunistic `flushQueue()` under `withContext(Dispatchers.IO)` so the user sees the entry leave the list without waiting for the next scheduled sync. Flush failures are swallowed with a warning log — the entry either completes, stays pending for the next tick, or lands back in dead-letter after N more transient failures. (c) **New screen** `ui/screens/sync/SyncIssuesScreen.kt` — Hilt-scoped `SyncIssuesViewModel` collects `observeDeadLetterEntries()` as a `StateFlow<List<SyncQueueEntity>>` via `stateIn(WhileSubscribed(5s))`, plus a `_retryingIds: Set<Long>` snapshot that tracks in-flight retries so the per-row OutlinedButton can show a 14dp CircularProgressIndicator + "Retrying…" label instead of the normal "Retry" icon while the DAO UPDATE + flush kick is pending. Screen renders a `LazyColumn` of `BrandCard` rows (matches the app's card surface pattern), each showing `"Type • operation"` heading + `DateFormatter.formatRelative(createdAt)` timestamp + `last_error` in error color (maxLines=2, ellipsis) + a trailing Retry button. `key = { it.id }` on `items(...)` so Compose reuses LayoutNodes across updates. Empty state: centered CheckCircle + "All synced" + "No pending sync failures." subcopy — appears instantly when the last entry is resurrected. No discard action — the 30-day retention sweep in `SyncManager.purgeOldDeadLetters()` is the only path that removes entries, intentional because a failed sync almost always represents work the user wants preserved (ticket / customer / note) and making discard easy-to-reach invites accidental data loss. (d) **Navigation** — added `Screen.SyncIssues : Screen("sync-issues")` to `AppNavGraph.kt`, registered the composable in the NavHost, and extended the bottom-nav hide rules so the diagnostic screen doesn't show the tab bar. (e) **Entry point** — `SettingsScreen.kt` gained a new `onSyncIssues: (() -> Unit)?` parameter plus `SettingsViewModel.deadLetterCount: StateFlow<Int>` from `syncQueueDao.getDeadLetterCount()` (new constructor-injected `SyncQueueDao` dependency; Hilt auto-wires via existing `DatabaseModule`). When count > 0, renders a new `SyncIssuesTileRow` above the existing Server-connection card: CloudOff icon in error color + "Sync issues" title + dynamic subtitle ("1 change failed to sync" / "N changes failed to sync") + trailing red pill-shaped Surface showing the count. Tile is hidden entirely when count is 0 — common healthy state is zero rows, user only ever sees it during actual failure.
